               <div class="post-content rich-text-styled" id="rgw11_59d37ce7064ca"> 
                <h1 class="topic-post-title"> Does anyone know of an alternative R package for sentiment analysis? </h1> 
                <div class="topic-post-text"> 
                 <p>Having&nbsp;recently started a text mining project, I have been struggling with an R package called 'sentiment' while performing a&nbsp;sentiment analysis. The package is only available in the archives of CRAN, seems outdated and was not compatible with the most recent version of R (on my computer). Does anyone know an alternative or even better R package for sentiment analysis?</p> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

                   <div id="rgw46_59d37ce7064ca" class="post-edit-content comment-body topic-post-text rich-text-styled"> 
                    <p>Hello,</p> 
                    <p>Maybe this discussion is outdated and you already found a good solution for your problem, but for those still interested in the topic, maybe you'll want to consider <em>syuzhet</em>.</p> 
                    <p>Relies on four (4) dictionaries and basically addresses the immediate needs for sentiment analysis and is up to date.</p> 
                    <p>Cheers!</p> 
                    <p>More info:<br><a href="https://www.researchgate.net/deref/https%3A%2F%2Fcran.r-project.org%2Fweb%2Fpackages%2Fsyuzhet%2Findex.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank">https://cran.r-project.org/web/packages/syuzhet/index.html</a></p> 
                   </div>
                  </div>

                    <p>You can also try using the older archived package called "Sentiment" which can be downloaded from here:&nbsp;<a href="https://www.researchgate.net/deref/http%3A%2F%2Fcran.r-project.org%2Fsrc%2Fcontrib%2FArchive%2Fsentiment%2F" rel="noopener" target="_blank">http://cran.r-project.org/src/contrib/Archive/sentiment/</a>.</p> 
                    <p>There's also the ViralHeat Sentiment API which can be used with R and R Studio:&nbsp;<a href="https://www.researchgate.net/deref/https%3A%2F%2Fwww.viralheat.com%2Fdata-apis%2F" rel="noopener" target="_blank">https://www.viralheat.com/data-apis/</a>.</p>

                 <div id="rgw66_59d37ce7064ca" class="react-container">

                   <div id="rgw67_59d37ce7064ca" class="post-edit-content comment-body topic-post-text rich-text-styled"> 
                    <p>There are various APIs for sentiment analysis you can use, see e.g. a list of APIs available on Mashape <a href="https://www.researchgate.net/deref/http%3A%2F%2Fblog.mashape.com%2Flist-of-20-sentiment-analysis-apis%2F" rel="noopener" target="_blank">http://blog.mashape.com/list-of-20-sentiment-analysis-apis/</a> Some of them are free, and some have a certain free usage allowance.</p> 
                    <p>You'd only need to write a client in R to interact with such a service. It is quite straightforward with the httr library (<a href="https://www.researchgate.net/deref/http%3A%2F%2Fcran.r-project.org%2Fweb%2Fpackages%2Fhttr%2Findex.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank">http://cran.r-project.org/web/packages/httr/index.html</a>).</p> 
                   </div>
                  </div>
                 </div>

                   <div id="rgw108_59d37ce7064ca" class="post-edit-content comment-body topic-post-text rich-text-styled"> 
                    <p>Hello,</p> 
                    <p>Maybe this discussion is outdated and you already found a good solution for your problem, but for those still interested in the topic, maybe you'll want to consider <em>syuzhet</em>.</p> 
                    <p>Relies on four (4) dictionaries and basically addresses the immediate needs for sentiment analysis and is up to date.</p> 
                    <p>Cheers!</p> 
                    <p>More info:<br><a href="https://www.researchgate.net/deref/https%3A%2F%2Fcran.r-project.org%2Fweb%2Fpackages%2Fsyuzhet%2Findex.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank">https://cran.r-project.org/web/packages/syuzhet/index.html</a></p> 
                   </div>
                  </div>
                 </div> 
                </div>
